<strong>Cast:</strong> Tobyey Maguire, Carey Mulligan, Joel Edgerton, Isla Fisher<br/>
<strong>Classification:</strong> M<br/>

<div id="theReview">
<h2>The Great Gatsby</h2>
<p class="ratd"> Rated <em>M</em></p>
<p><em>Review by David Stratton</em></p>
<p>Many believe F. Scott Fitzgerald's THE GREAT GATSBY, published in 1925, is The Great American Novel, but filming this story of a mysterious, and mysteriously romantic, millionaire who acquires a home across the water from the married woman he's loved for years, has proved a tricky proposition. The version made in 1926 with Warner Baxter survives only in a trailer, which suggests the party scenes were the main focus; the 1949 version, with Alan Ladd, is interested in filling in Gatsby's background and features elements Fitzgerald only hinted at, while the 1974 version, faithful, beautiful, star-studded and a bit dull, brought the career of the talented Jack Clayton to a halt. And now comes Baz Luhrmann's version, with Leonardo DiCaprio as Gatsby, Carey Mulligan as Daisy, Joel Edgerton as her faithless husband, Tom, and Tobey Maguire as Nick, through whose observant eyes the story unfolds..<br/><br/>Luhrmann's film has been, and will be, attacked for all sorts of reasons, but let's be positive about it. After all, Fitzgerald isn't holy writ, any more than Shakespeare is, and this is Luhrmann's approach to the story - you wouldn't expect him to take the sort of sober approach Clayton did because, before all else, Luhrmann is a showman, he loves the razzle-dazzle, the excess. So this is a lavish Gatsby, an extreme Gatsby, a 3D Gatsby and - if you allow yourself - an entertaining Gatsby, with some terrific performances, wonderfully elaborate scenes, and a love of cinema evident in every frame - a love of Big Cinema, DeMille cinema, because though I think Luhrmann captures the essence of the story his approach, as we always knew it would be, is on a very grand scale.</p>
<h2>Further comments</h2>
<p>DAVID: Margaret?<br/><br/>MARGARET: Yes, he is. He is an operatic director, a theatrical director operating ...<br/><br/>DAVID: It's almost a musical actually.<br/><br/>MARGARET: Well, yes, operating in a film medium and I think this suits material that comes from a theatrical background. Like ROMEO AND JULIET is a fantastic film. STRICTLY BALLROOM was an adaptation from stage. I'm not sure that his approach suits the delicacy and elusiveness of Fitzgerald's novel, which I have to admit I loved and is very precious to me. <br/><br/>DAVID: Great Gatsby was adapted for the stage at the very beginning. George Cukor directed the original Broadway production.<br/><br/>MARGARET: I don't care. I think everybody has got to be very careful with this material and it is very delicate. It is very elusive.<br/><br/>DAVID: But why not give it this...<br/><br/>MARGARET: Well, you can but, in fact, what's beautiful about it is the prose and also this sense of yearning that permeates the novel and that really only comes in hinted at in the second half of the film. I do think that Leonardo DiCaprio is wonderful as Gatsby. He's the only thing that gives this film heart.<br/><br/>DAVID: I think Joel Edgerton is very good too.<br/><br/>MARGARET: I think Joel is excellent in it. I think Tobey Maguire is a truly boring actor and his voice, which is used so much in voice over in this film, is so - I think I just hated that bit of casting.<br/><br/>DAVID: I think Nick is a rather boring character or potentially a rather boring character.<br/><br/>MARGARET: Well, but it's his yearning too that, you know, he wants ...<br/><br/>DAVID: I think Tobey Maguire does that quite well. <br/><br/>MARGARET: Well, we disagree. We disagree. Look, I think it's really hard to look at a film of a book that you've really taken to heart. I'm giving this three stars.<br/><br/>DAVID: I'm giving it three and a half.<br/></p>

<h3>Bre :</h3>
<p class="date">14 Jul 2014 2:55:53am</p>
<p class="comment">((The Great Gatsby))[[8]]<br>When I first watched the movie I had lost interest and tuned out halfway, however after being coerced into watching it again (and to the end) by family I quickly developed a love for the film. It was unique and vibrant, and though it may not have achieved the same level of depth as the book (which most movie adaptions fail to do anyway) it still proved to be facinating on multiple levels and forced me to watch it a third time to truly understand the complexities of each character. Great film!</br></p>

<h3>Sarah :</h3>
<p class="date">19 Oct 2013 12:40:29pm</p>
<p class="comment">((The Great Gatsby))[[3]]<br>I studied this book in year 12 and it is a favourite. I wanted to feel like as I did when I  finished the book years ago - I didn't. The film had me asking "what was so great about Gatsby, really?".  He was an obsessive stalker, self absorbed and a rich dodgy businessman. When Nick, yells "they're a rotten crowd... your worth the whole damn bunch put together", I asked myself "why exactly?".  The greatest lines of the film ,were ruined with cheesy montage/text overlay, I cringed and doubted my love of the book. Stars for Joel's awesome Tom.</br></p>

<p class="date">19 Aug 2013 2:31:51pm</p>
<p class="comment">((The Great Gatsby))[[2]]<br>Like a red shiny supermarket apple when you take a bite it's bland and soggy, all packaging and no substance. Intoning Gatsby like a reverent mantra interspersed with "old sport" and constantly zooming in on the accoutrements of wealth cannot hide the fact that this a second rate soapy which would bomb in Rio where they do it so much better.<br>Baz  should have been booed off the stage after the fiascos of Australia and Moulin Rouge but the master of camp surfaces again. <h3>i.n.c.o.g.n.i.t.o :</h3>
<p class="date">01 Aug 2013 10:15:17pm</p>
<p class="comment">((The Great Gatsby))[[7]]<br>The costumes, incredible.  The music, impressive.  The sets, fantastic.  Attention to detail was usually good, but some  subtleties... appalling.  With such a large budget, at least make that photo of Gatsby could've looked real, not superimposed, and the medal could've realistic engraving, not just a font off Word!  The CGI was very fake at times, and Baz tried to sneakily reuse film footage.  But I was swept along into the fast paced world of Gatsby, and I didn't find myself checking my watch during this film.  You'll either love it or hate it.  I'm somewhere in between: it's quite good.<br/></br></p>

<h3>Haden :</h3>
<p class="date">26 Jun 2013 2:17:39am</p>
<p class="comment">((The Great Gatsby))[[9]]<br/>No-one seems to be commenting that this's a continuation of Baz's beloved theme, ''my only love sprung from my only hate'', a la 'R+J' &amp; 'Moulin Rouge', 'GG' serving as its vehicle this time and Tom being the Maharaja. For thosem who either look for or are aware of it, quite deep, cosmic 'Titanic'/'Moulin Rouge'-esque background theme of the transformative power of love, framed with somewhat mystical visual and verbal references to the stars. Gorgeous use of NYC visuals, elaborate and extraordinarily detailed, much fine acting and I think Toby Maguire is quite sensitive and gentle an acting presence myself.</p>

<a id="m_ucMessageDisplay22401_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m22401"></a>
<h3>sj :</h3>
<p class="date">10 Jun 2013 6:52:26pm</p>
<p class="comment">((The Great Gatsby))[[8]]<br/>I think Luhrmann perfectly captures the schizophrenic, excessive superficial and idealistic atmosphere of the 1920's. This was a decade were the horrors of WW1 were flung off and replaced by excess and frivolity. Youth and beauty and the promise of meritocratic wealth were the gods of the time, yet in the shadows still lurked class dichotomies, and socio-religous morality that pervaded this sense of idealism. Luhrmann's captures this feverish and idealistic decade well, the over the top images creates the feeling of the hyper-real, a simulation of reality that people believe is real but is only a projection-a dream. Fabulous!</p>
<p class="links">
<a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20141224201317/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/AlertModerator.aspx?b=117&amp;m=22401&amp;tpa=&amp;r=%2ftmb%2fView%2fMessage.aspx%3fb%3d117%26t%3d725%26a%3d0%26ps%3d50%26tpa%3d%26uto%3d1%26dm%3d4%26ci%3d0%26pd%3d1%26so%3dDateTime%26soa%3dFalse%26p%3d1%26p2%3d0" onclick="return popup(this.href);">Alert moderator</a>

Just re-read the book in May, and realised I'd  forgotten what happens, but didn't really feel the imagery as much as I'd remembered it affecting me in high school.  But tonight I saw Baz Luhrmann's rendering and was blown away.  I find his movies a bit too emotive and arty for my practical self, but with Great Gatsby I felt that Baz had brought the imagery out way, way better than my tired old imagination had, and I was 17 again.  Great job.  Fabulous!</p>

<h3>Brutus :</h3>
<p class="date">06 Jun 2013 1:01:53pm</p>
<p class="comment">((The Great Gatsby))[[8]]<br/>The essential point is that the previous versions (particularly the Redford one) were altogether too reverential and respectful of the "Great American Novel" schtick  - and basically rather dull as a result.  The bottom line is that Gatsby is a deluded (albeit romantic) social climber, and Daisy, frankly, is a bit of a pain.  Baz (very sensibly in my view) has simply decided to jazz the whole thing up and make it more entertaining, with modern music and the like.  A better film than it is getting credit for. Cinematic and contemporary.</p>

<li>
<a id="m_ucMessageDisplay22271_m_anchMessageAnchor" name="m22271"></a>
<h3>Carli :</h3>
<p class="date">05 Jun 2013 4:32:50pm</p>
<p class="comment">((The Great Gatsby))[[7]]<br/>I found the movie stunningly beautiful, visually, and was prepared that there might be more caricature than character development. Nevertheless I couldn't help but imagine what a more soulful actor could have done for the role of Nick Carraway. The novel is a secret love story told amidst the loud and roaring 20s, whereas this version is the opposite.<br/><br/>I'm not sure why Baz said this movie is 'where we are now' given that the 1920s were a decade of decadence and prosperity in America, but it was great fun to take a nostalgic trip to better times.</p>
<p class="links">

<h3>JC :</h3>
<p class="date">05 Jun 2013 10:30:03am</p>
<p class="comment">((The Great Gatsby))[[2]]<br/>I never read the book and I'm not american so I didn't care less about how close to it the film was. But Luhrmann's approach was for me over the top. I was expecting him to resurrect the era with music of the time, background political stuff, social changes in society, good dialogues etc.<br/>But all I got was a visual firework in 3 D. The music reminded me of Rap and House music. The actors were overacting, except Leonardo DiCaprio who was as good as he always is.<br/>A missed opportunity, almost as bad as Luhrmann's Australia!</p>

<h3>harry georgatos :</h3>
<p class="date">05 Jun 2013 8:53:30am</p>
<p class="comment">((The Great Gatsby))[[7]]<br/>Purists should look elsewhere even though Luhrmann gets to the core of the novel. This is a Luhrmann film first and foremost. The 3D visual spectacle is overwhelming as it is a film of sight and sound. Not as bombastic as MOULIN ROUGE but a 1920's rollercoaster ride never-the-less. This is Luhrmann best film since ROMEO AND JULIET. Still I would have modernised the story as Lurhmann did with ROMEO AND JULIET. It took me years to appreciate the brilliance of MOULIN ROUGE where GATSBY was an instant pleasure!</p>

<h3>Daniel Spicer :</h3>
<p class="date">04 Jun 2013 11:27:03pm</p>
<p class="comment">((The Great Gatsby))[[6]]<br/>This film could have been edited down about half an hour or more, it really wears on your patience because there aren't a lot of plot complications. I was sometimes bored, but thankfully the performances are engaging enough to carry the film. Even if they were superficially-developed characters, I think that was the point. I guess the aspect that won me over were the visuals - they're always dazzling, with a kind of glossiness that looks artificial, but helped create a mood opposed to my regular indifference.</p>

<h3>Lex :</h3>
<p class="date">04 Jun 2013 10:42:37pm</p>
<p class="comment">((The Great Gatsby))[[8]]<br/>Bravo Baz Luhrmann for capturing the frivolity and shallow self centredness of the Flapper generation. This film is faithful to the novel and while we hear critics insist a film fails if the screen image falls short of the magic of the written word, Baz has delivered as well as any film maker can. The acting is high quality exceeding that of Redford and Farrow in the 1974 version. As for the directorial lavishness that has been criticised, I applaud such excess.as an accurate interpretation of the era. Baz Luhrmann has done us proud. Your best yet.</p>
<p class="links">

<script language="JavaScript" type="text/javascript">


var newtopicKey;

$(document).ready(function(){

audShow();
changeAction();
formatComments();

// end ready
});	

function audShow() {
	// display word count only if js enabled
	document.getElementById("wordCount").style.display='inline';
	document.getElementById("audiencecomment").style.display='block';
	if (document.getElementById("allnewComments")) {
		document.getElementById("allnewComments").innerHTML = document.getElementById("loadComments").innerHTML;
	}
}


function changeAction() {
	// avoids non-js form submission 
	var tmpStoryid = "??StoryID??";
	if (document.m_frmMainForm) {
		document.m_frmMainForm.action = 'https://web.archive.org/web/20141224201317/http://www2b.abc.net.au/tmb/View/NewMessage.aspx?b=117&amp;tn='+tmpStoryid+'&amp;dm=1&amp;tpa=&amp;r=&amp;layout=popup';
		}
}



function formatComments() {
	// replace H3 tag with 'Name:' + name
	var arrayH3 = document.getElementById("comments").getElementsByTagName("h3");
	for (var i = 0; i < arrayH3.length; i++) {
		var theString = arrayH3[i].innerHTML;
		theString = theString.replace(":", "");
		theString = "Name: "+theString;
		arrayH3[i].innerHTML = 	theString;
	}
	// add rating value to each comment
	var arrayComment = getElementsByClassName( 'comment', 'p' );	
	for (var c = 0; c < arrayComment.length; c++) {
		var theComment = arrayComment[c].innerHTML;
		theComment = theComment.replace("[[", "<span class='userRating'>Rating: <img src='https://web.archive.org/web/20141224201317/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/audience/stars").replace("]]",".png' alt='rating'></span>").replace("((", "<!-- ").replace(")))", "))").replace("))", "-->");
		arrayComment[c].innerHTML = theComment;
	}

	
}


function formCheck(zeForm) {
	// pass key to form
	document.getElementById("keyField").value = newtopicKey;
	// basic validation
	if (document.getElementById("yname").value.length < 1) {
		alert("Please enter your name or nickname.");
		document.getElementById("yname").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;
	}
	if (document.getElementById("yemail").value.length < 6) {
		alert("Please enter a valid email address.");
		document.getElementById("yemail").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;
	}
	if (zeForm.score.options[0].selected && zeForm.score.options[0].value=="na") {
		alert("You forgot to rate the movie!");
		document.getElementById("score").style.background='#FFFDC8';	
		return false;
	}	
	// check for http
	spamcheck=zeForm.m_tbxText.value;
	if (spamcheck.indexOf("http")!=-1) {
		document.m_frmMainForm.action = 'https://web.archive.org/web/20141224201317/http://www.abc.net.au/atthemovies/audience/blank.htm';
	}
	// check word count
	wct = cnt(zeForm.m_tbxText.value);
	if (wct > 100) {
		alert("Comments are limited to 100 words. You've written "+wct+" words!");
		document.getElementById("remark").style.background='#FFFDC8';
		return false;	
	}
	
	// replace usual suspect bad characters 
	badChars = Array  ('', '', '', '', '', 'ö', 'é', 'è', 'ñ', 'â', ' ', '','','´');
	goodChars = Array ('...', '-', '-', '"', '"', 'o', 'e', 'e', 'n', 'a', ' ', '\'','\'','\'');
	fld = document.getElementById("remark");
	for(i=0;i<badChars.length;i++){
		restring = new RegExp( badChars[i] , 'g');
		fld.value = fld.value.replace(restring,goodChars[i]);
	}
	fldn = document.getElementById("yname");
	for(j=0;j<badChars.length;j++){
		restringj = new RegExp( badChars[j] , 'g');
		fldn.value = fldn.value.replace(restringj,goodChars[j]);
	}	
	
	// add rating to comment field in [[ ]] tags 
	var theSel = zeForm.score.selectedIndex;
	var theRating = zeForm.score[theSel].value; 
	zeForm.m_tbxText.value = "[["+theRating+"]]\n" + zeForm.m_tbxText.value;
	
	// add movie title to comment field in (( )) tags 
	zeForm.m_tbxText.value = "(("+theMovie+"))" + zeForm.m_tbxText.value;	
	
	// display thankyou div layer and hide form. 
	document.getElementById("favFormThx").style.display='block';
	document.getElementById("favForm").style.display='none';
	document.getElementById("wordCount").style.display='none';	
	
	// all clear, submit the form
	return true;
}

// word count function
function cnt(theform){
	var y=theform;
	var r = 0;
	a=y.replace('\n',' ');
	a=a.split(' ');
	for (z=0; z<a.length; z++) {if (a[z].length > 0) r++;}
	return r;
}

function remainingWords(textAreaContent,textAreaContentValue, maxWords) 
{
	// Determine the number of words we have left
	var numberofwords = cnt(textAreaContentValue);
	wordsLeft = maxWords - numberofwords;
	if (wordsLeft < 1)
	{	// if 100 change color to red
		document.getElementById("wcNum").style.color='red'; 
	} else {
		document.getElementById("wcNum").style.color='#ffffff'; 
	}
	// update word count number
	document.getElementById("wcNum").innerHTML=(0+numberofwords);
}

// windows media alt box
function showWindows() {
	document.getElementById("windowsMed").style.display='block';
}


// generic get by class name
function getElementsByClassName(strClass, strTag, objContElm) {
  strTag = strTag || "*";
  objContElm = objContElm || document;    
  var objColl = objContElm.getElementsByTagName(strTag);
  if (!objColl.length &&  strTag == "*" &&  objContElm.all) objColl = objContElm.all;
  var arr = new Array();                              
  var delim = strClass.indexOf('|') != -1  ? '|' : ' ';   
  var arrClass = strClass.split(delim);    
  for (var i = 0, j = objColl.length; i < j; i++) {                         
    var arrObjClass = objColl[i].className.split(' ');   
    if (delim == ' ' && arrClass.length > arrObjClass.length) continue;
    var c = 0;
    comparisonLoop:
    for (var k = 0, l = arrObjClass.length; k < l; k++) {
      for (var m = 0, n = arrClass.length; m < n; m++) {
        if (arrClass[m] == arrObjClass[k]) c++;
        if ((delim == '|' && c == 1) || (delim == ' ' && c == arrClass.length)) {
          arr.push(objColl[i]); 
          break comparisonLoop;
        }
      }
    }
  }
  return arr; 
}

// called from 'new discussion' page in iframe
function sayHello(theKey) {
	newtopicKey = theKey;
}

// talk to www2b iframe
document.domain = "abc.net.au";

// end ready
});
